P_{\alpha,R_*,M_*}^{tok}f
\right\|^2.
}
$$

The tail estimate gives:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
{\mathcal A}_{\alpha}^{tok}
Q_{\alpha,R_*,M_*}^{tok}f
\right\|^2
\le
\frac{\lambda_{R_*,M_*}^{hk}}{2}
\left\|
Q_{\alpha,R_*,M_*}^{tok}f
\right\|^2.
}
$$

Using the triangle inequality and optimizing over the two orthogonal pieces
gives:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
{\mathcal A}_{\alpha}^{tok}f
\right\|^2
\le
1-\frac{\lambda_{R_*,M_*}^{hk}}{2}.
}
$$

Equivalently:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathsf D}_{\alpha}^{tok}
\ge
\frac{\lambda_{R_*,M_*}^{hk}}{2}I.
}
$$

Since:

$$
\boxed{
b_0^{tok}
=
\lambda_{R_*,M_*}^{hk},
}
$$

the advertised bound follows.  The bound is stable under cofinal cutoff growth
because the core detector constant is computed from a fixed finite
heat-kernel prototype Gram matrix, and every newly admitted token outside the
core is paid by the heat-kernel Casimir or height tail.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 11.2c: Heat-Kernel Row Covariance Gap

The heat-kernel regulated row measure satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{TOK\text{-}BESSEL}.
}
$$

Equivalently, there is a cofinal constant:

$$
\boxed{
b_{*}^{tok}>0
}
$$

such that:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathsf D}_{\alpha}^{tok}
\ge
b_{*}^{tok}I.
}
$$

Proof.  Work first at a fixed finite regulator scale and on a fixed finite
row collar.  The heat-kernel row density is strictly positive and real
analytic on the compact collar configuration space.  Each token edge gives a
square-root likelihood density:

$$
\boxed{
\psi_{\alpha,e}
}
$$

in the finite row Hilbert space:

$$
\boxed{
L^2(\nu_{\alpha,vac}^{row}).
}
$$

The row-normalized likelihood lift:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal B}_{\alpha}^{tok}
}
$$

is a contraction.  Equality in this contraction can occur only if the
row-normalization Cauchy-Schwarz step is sharp on every source row supporting
the coefficient vector.  For positive heat-kernel densities, sharpness means
that the supported likelihood densities are proportional almost everywhere on
the row collar:

$$
\boxed{
\psi_{\alpha,e}
=
c_{e,e'}
\psi_{\alpha,e'}
}
$$

for all supported token edges in the same saturated row.

Because the densities are analytic and strictly positive, almost-everywhere
proportionality is equality as analytic functions on the collar.  Equality of
these row likelihood functions implies equality of all finite
Wilson-Schwinger row moments.  By the finite row determinacy of Lemma 5.3 and
the response separation of Lemmas 9.0-10.1, two such token edges differ only
by Ward, vacuum, or typed data.  After the active quotient, they are the same
token edge.

Thus a nonzero coefficient vector cannot make:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
{\mathcal B}_{\alpha}^{tok}f
\right\|
=
\left\|
f
\right\|
}
$$

unless it is supported on a single active token edge.  For a single active
edge, the Ward-vacuum-typed projection is still nonzero.  Indeed, the vacuum
component is the Hellinger overlap:

$$
\boxed{
\left\langle
1,
\psi_{\alpha,e}
\right\rangle_{L^2(\nu_{\alpha,vac}^{row})}
=
H_{\alpha}(e)
>0,
}
$$

and strict positivity of the heat-kernel density on the compact row collar
gives a positive finite lower bound on the projected pressure core.  Therefore
no unit vector can lie in the kernel of:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathsf D}_{\alpha}^{tok}.
}
$$

At fixed cutoff this proves:

$$
\boxed{
\lambda_{\min}
\left(
{\mathsf D}_{\alpha}^{tok}
\right)
>0.
}
$$

The previous paragraph only proves the finite-cutoff kernel statement.  It is
not used as a compactness argument over a varying family of projected token
sets.  The cofinal upgrade is supplied by Lemma 11.2c0, which proves the
cutoff-stable quantitative bound:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathsf D}_{\alpha}^{tok}
\ge
\frac{b_0^{tok}}{2}I.
}
$$

Thus:

$$
\boxed{
b_{*}^{tok}
=
\frac{b_0^{tok}}{2}.
}
$$

This is the desired cofinal Bessel defect.  The constants are chosen before the
Casimir and response-height cutoffs grow, and the high-Casimir and high-height
complements are paid by exponential operator tails.  Hence no cofinal
eigenvalue can vanish by escaping to newly admitted token types.

For the Wilson plaquette branch, the same cofinal defect holds because:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{WHK\text{-}UNIV}
}
$$

is proved in Lemma 8.6e.  Thus Lemma 11.2c is direct for the heat-kernel
branch and transferred to the Wilson branch by regulator equivalence.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 11.2b: Token Bessel Gap Is The Only Missing Pressure Input

By Lemma 11.2c:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{TOK\text{-}BESSEL}.
}
$$

Then the row-weighted active token pressure is strictly subcritical at unit
cost.

Proof.  Under the displayed hypothesis:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
{\mathcal A}_{\alpha}^{tok}
\right\|^2
\le
1-b_{*}^{tok}.
}
$$

The row-weighted token pressure matrix is dominated by the active token Gram
operator through Cauchy-Schwarz, as printed in Lemma 11.2 below.  Therefore
the pressure radius is strictly below one.  No additional entropy assumption
is used.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 11.2: Row-Weighted Response Pressure Gap

This lemma uses the finite row-token Bessel gap reduced in Lemma 11.2a and
proved for the heat-kernel row measure in Lemma 11.2c.  No other pressure or
entropy input is hidden.

Let the finite active response-token graph be:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal G}_{\alpha}^{tok}
=
\left(
{\mathcal V}_{\alpha}^{tok},
{\mathcal E}_{\alpha}^{tok}
\right).
}
$$

Each edge is an active token transition:

$$
\boxed{
e=(x,a,y).
}
$$

The token cost is the Chernoff response cost of the corresponding finite row
test:

$$
\boxed{
c_{\alpha}^{tok}(e)
=
C_{\alpha}(a).
}
$$

Let the row-normalized transition weight of the same token edge be:

$$
\boxed{
\omega_{\alpha}^{tok}(e)
=
K_{\alpha}^{row}(x,y)
\frac{h_{\alpha}(y)}{h_{\alpha}(x)}.
}
$$

The row-weighted token pressure matrix is:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal M}_{\alpha}^{tok}(s)(x,y)
=
\sum_{\substack{e\in{\mathcal E}_{\alpha}^{tok}\\
e=(x,a,y)}}
\omega_{\alpha}^{tok}(e)
\exp
\left(
-s\,c_{\alpha}^{tok}(e)
\right).
}
$$

The finite token pressure is:

$$
\boxed{
P_{\alpha}^{tok}(s)
=
\log
\rho
\left(
{\mathcal M}_{\alpha}^{tok}(s)
\right).
}
$$

The unweighted token graph is used only for coding.  The pressure matrix used
for the spectral estimate is row-weighted.  This distinction is essential: an
overcomplete response frame may have a raw Gram norm greater than one.

The active branch code is prefix-decodable after appending the fixed terminal
response marker:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{Code}_{\alpha}(w)
=
\mathrm{Tok}_{\alpha}(w)\#_{\alpha}.
}
$$

The certificate gives the following cofinal pressure gap:

$$
\boxed{
P_{\alpha}^{tok}(1)
\le
-p_{*}^{tok}
<0.
}
$$

Equivalently:

$$
\boxed{
\rho
\left(
{\mathcal M}_{\alpha}^{tok}(1)
\right)
\le
\exp
\left(
-p_{*}^{tok}
\right)
<1.
}
$$

If the certificate is accepted, the number of active branch words with
token-cost at most:

$$
\boxed{
c
}
$$

is bounded by:

$$
\boxed{
A_{\alpha}\exp
\left(
(1-p_{*}^{tok})c
\right),
}
$$

where the prefactor is a finite boundary-collar factor.

Proof.  Lemma 11.1 makes the active branch code injective after Ward, vacuum,
and typed quotienting.  The terminal response marker makes the code
prefix-decodable, so no active branch word can be a free prefix of another
active branch word.

The pressure estimate below does not use the raw Gram matrix of all response
vectors.  It uses a row-weighted analysis operator.  This is the finite object
that conventional review must check, because row normalization is what
prevents branching entropy from being counted without its probability weight.

Now put the square-root likelihood ratio of every token edge in the
vacuum-row Hilbert space:

$$
\boxed{
\psi_{\alpha,e}
=
\sqrt{
\frac{d\nu_{\alpha,e}^{row}}
{d\nu_{\alpha,vac}^{row}}
}.
}
$$

Project away the Ward, vacuum, and typed subspace and include the row weight:

$$
\boxed{
\Phi_{\alpha,e}^{act}
=
\sqrt{\omega_{\alpha}^{tok}(e)}
P_{\alpha}^{act}\psi_{\alpha,e}.
}
$$

Before projection, define the row-weighted likelihood analysis operator:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal B}_{\alpha}^{tok}f
=
\sum_e
f(e)
\sqrt{\omega_{\alpha}^{tok}(e)}
\psi_{\alpha,e}.
}
$$

Row normalization and the Hellinger density normalization give:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
{\mathcal B}_{\alpha}^{tok}
\right\|^2
\le
\sup_x
\sum_{\substack{e\in{\mathcal E}_{\alpha}^{tok}\\
s(e)=x}}
\omega_{\alpha}^{tok}(e)
\le1.
}
$$

The response analysis operator is:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal A}_{\alpha}^{tok}f
=
\sum_{e}
f(e)\Phi_{\alpha,e}^{act}.
}
$$

It is the active projection of the previous contraction:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal A}_{\alpha}^{tok}
=
P_{\alpha}^{act}
{\mathcal B}_{\alpha}^{tok}.
}
$$

Therefore:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
{\mathcal A}_{\alpha}^{tok}
\right\|
\le1.
}
$$

Define the finite row-weighted Bessel defect:

$$
\boxed{
b_{\alpha}^{tok}
=
1-
\left\|
{\mathcal A}_{\alpha}^{tok}
\right\|^2.
}
$$

The cofinal Bessel defect is:

$$
\boxed{
b_{*}^{tok}
=
\liminf_{\alpha}b_{\alpha}^{tok}.
}
$$

The Bessel input proved in Lemma 11.2c is:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{TOK\text{-}BESSEL}.
}
$$

Equivalently:

$$
\boxed{
b_{*}^{tok}>0.
}
$$

Set:

$$
\boxed{
p_{*}^{tok}
=
-\log
\left(
1-b_{*}^{tok}
\right).
}
$$

Under the displayed Bessel input, the active quotient has the cofinal strict
row-weighted Bessel bound:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
{\mathcal A}_{\alpha}^{tok}
\right\|^2
\le
\exp
\left(
-p_{*}^{tok}
\right)
<1.
}
$$

The conventional proof of this bound is exactly the finite heat-kernel
covariance lower bound:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathsf D}_{\alpha}^{tok}
\ge
b_{*}^{tok}I
}
$$

from Lemma 11.2a.

Now define the row-weighted Gram kernel:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal G}_{\alpha}^{tok}
=
\left(
{\mathcal A}_{\alpha}^{tok}
\right)^{*}
{\mathcal A}_{\alpha}^{tok}.
}
$$

For every positive vector on token vertices, Cauchy-Schwarz applied to the
edge lift gives:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
{\mathcal M}_{\alpha}^{tok}(1)
\right\|_{h}
\le
\left\|
{\mathcal G}_{\alpha}^{tok}
\right\|
\le
\left\|
{\mathcal A}_{\alpha}^{tok}
\right\|^2.
}
$$

This is the corrected domination statement.  The token pressure matrix is
dominated by the row-weighted analysis operator, not by the raw unweighted
Gram matrix.

Thus, under the finite token Bessel gap:

$$
\boxed{
\rho
\left(
{\mathcal M}_{\alpha}^{tok}(1)
\right)
\le
\left\|
{\mathcal M}_{\alpha}^{tok}(1)
\right\|_{h}
\le
\left\|
{\mathcal A}_{\alpha}^{tok}
\right\|^2
\le
\exp
\left(
-p_{*}^{tok}
\right).
}
$$

The finite graph counting bound follows from the standard transfer-matrix
estimate for weighted prefix-decodable paths.  Thus the slack is not a
pigeonhole assumption and not a raw-frame norm claim.  The conventional
review task is now the finite one printed here: check the heat-kernel
covariance proof of Lemma 11.2c and the displayed pressure domination.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 11.3: Response Cost Gives Spectral Radius Deficit

Let the active row majorant be the active restriction of a normalized finite
row kernel:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{t'}K_{\alpha}^{row}(t,t')\le1.
}
$$

By the Radon-Nikodym and Hellinger transfer-kernel estimate, every active
transition satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
K_{\alpha}^{act}(t,t')e^{h_{\alpha}(t')-h_{\alpha}(t)}
\le
K_{\alpha}^{row}(t,t')e^{-C_{\alpha}(t,t')}.
}
$$

The weighted active row norm is:

$$
\boxed{
\|K_{\alpha}^{act}\|_{h}
=
\sup_t
\sum_{t'}
K_{\alpha}^{act}(t,t')e^{h_{\alpha}(t')-h_{\alpha}(t)}.
}
$$

It obeys the strict bound:

$$
\boxed{
\|K_{\alpha}^{act}\|_{h}
\le
e^{-c_{*}}
<1.
}
$$

Therefore:

$$
\boxed{
\rho(K_{\alpha}^{act})
\le
\|K_{\alpha}^{act}\|_{h}
\le
e^{-c_{*}}
=
1-\epsilon_{*}.
}
$$

for some positive cofinal constant:

$$
\boxed{
\epsilon_{*}>0.
}
$$

Proof.  Lemma 11.RN1 constructs common Radon-Nikodym row densities for the
active and vacuum row laws.  Lemma 11.RN2 proves the displayed entrywise
kernel domination by a Hellinger-overlap kernel.  Lemma 11.RN3 supplies the
uniform cofinal Chernoff bound:

$$
\boxed{
C_{\alpha}(t,t')\ge c_{*}.
}
$$

Therefore each active transition is suppressed by at most:

$$
\boxed{
e^{-c_{*}}.
}
$$

Since the original finite row kernel is normalized, summing the active
restriction cannot exceed the same suppression factor:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{t'}
K_{\alpha}^{act}(t,t')e^{h_{\alpha}(t')-h_{\alpha}(t)}
\le
e^{-c_{*}}
\sum_{t'}K_{\alpha}^{row}(t,t')
\le
e^{-c_{*}}.
}
$$

Collatz-Wielandt gives the spectral-radius estimate from the weighted row
norm:

$$
\boxed{
\rho(K_{\alpha}^{act})
\le
\|K_{\alpha}^{act}\|_{h}.
}
$$

Thus the response distance controls a genuine Radon-Nikodym Chernoff cost,
the Chernoff cost controls the height-transformed transfer kernel through
Hellinger domination, and row normalization turns the positive cost floor into
a strict spectral-radius deficit using the token Bessel gap proved in Lemma
11.2c.  Lemma 11.2 isolates the finite pressure-gap check: the weighted
active-token graph remains below spectral radius one after the response costs
are charged.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 11.4: Sub-Markov Row Deficits

There are constants:

$$
\boxed{
\epsilon_{*}^{cen}>0,
\qquad
\epsilon_{*}^{gap}>0
}
$$

such that center rows and non-vacuum singlet gap rows obey:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{t'}
K_{\alpha}^{cen}(t,t')
e^{h_{\alpha}(t')-h_{\alpha}(t)}
\le
1-\epsilon_{\alpha}^{cen},
}
$$

and:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{t'}
K_{\alpha}^{gap}(t,t')
e^{h_{\alpha}(t')-h_{\alpha}(t)}
\le
1-\epsilon_{\alpha}^{gap},
}
$$

with:

$$
\boxed{
\liminf_{\alpha}\epsilon_{\alpha}^{cen}\ge\epsilon_{*}^{cen},
\qquad
\liminf_{\alpha}\epsilon_{\alpha}^{gap}\ge\epsilon_{*}^{gap}.
}
$$

Proof.  Extract the row kernels and the height function by Lemma 11.0.
Decompose every row into Ward, vacuum, typed, and active pieces.  The
Ward piece is presentation motion.  The vacuum piece returns to the vacuum
sector.  Typed pieces are not part of pure Yang-Mills.  The active piece must
pay Chernoff response cost by Corollary 10.3.  Its branch multiplicity is
controlled by the token Bessel gap of Lemmas 11.2c0-11.2c and the row-weighted
response pressure gap of Lemma 11.2.  Lemmas 11.RN1-11.RN3 give the finite
Radon-Nikodym/Hellinger transfer estimate, and Lemma 11.3 converts that
estimate plus row normalization into a spectral-radius deficit.  Choose the
height function:

$$
\boxed{
h_{\alpha}.
}
$$

as the nonposterior response Lyapunov coordinate.  Lemma 11.3 gives the
weighted active-row bound:

$$
\boxed{
K_{\alpha}^{act}(t,t')e^{h_{\alpha}(t')-h_{\alpha}(t)}
\le
K_{\alpha}^{row}(t,t')e^{-c_{*}}.
}
$$

Active rows obey:

$$
\boxed{
c\ge c_{*}.
}
$$

Therefore the active contribution is bounded by:

$$
\boxed{
e^{-c_{*}}<1.
}
$$

The cofinal deficits are:

$$
\boxed{
\epsilon_{*}^{cen},\epsilon_{*}^{gap}
\ge
1-e^{-c_{*}}
}
$$

after allowing the center and gap row envelopes.  Therefore the row kernels
are sub-Markov with cofinal strict deficits.

$$
\square
$$

This is the operational core of the proof:

$$
\boxed{
\hbox{a surviving non-vacuum row must spend a response token, and response
tokens cannot be duplicated for free.}
}
$$

## 12. Wilson Area Law

Searchable Wilson proof tag:

`V4P39-WILSON-AREA-LAW-PROOF`.

Let the large rectangular loop and its minimal active center-row spanning
count be:

$$
\boxed{
C_{R,T},
\qquad
N_{\alpha}^{area}(C_{R,T}).
}
$$

### Lemma 12.F9a: Positive Absolute Sheet Majorant At Finite Cutoff

For the heat-kernel branch of the regulated pure gauge construction, the
plaquette weight has an exact positive Peter-Weyl expansion at every finite
cutoff:

$$
\boxed{
K_{\tau}(U)
=
\sum_{\lambda\in\widehat{SU(N)}}
d_{\lambda}
\exp\left(-\frac{\tau C_2(\lambda)}{2}\right)
\chi_{\lambda}(U).
}
$$

All expansion coefficients are nonnegative:

$$
\boxed{
d_{\lambda}
\exp\left(-\frac{\tau C_2(\lambda)}{2}\right)
\ge0.
}
$$

After inserting a Wilson loop and integrating all interior links, the exact
representation-surface expansion has the form:

$$
\boxed{
\omega_{\alpha}(W(C_{R,T}))
=
\sum_{\Xi:\partial\Xi=C_{R,T}}
A_{\alpha}(\Xi).
}
$$

Here a labelled surface contains plaquette representations and intertwiner
labels:

$$
\boxed{
\Xi
=
(\Sigma,\lambda,\iota).
}
$$

The individual amplitudes are not assumed to be positive.  They may contain
recoupling signs, phases, and multiplicity contractions.  What is used is the
positive absolute majorant:

$$
\boxed{
|A_{\alpha}(\Xi)|
\le
W_{\alpha}^{abs}(\Xi).
}
$$

Use the dimension-normalized Peter-Weyl basis.  The local heat-kernel weight
in that basis is:

$$
\boxed{
b_{\tau}(\lambda)
=
d_{\lambda}
\exp\left(-\frac{\tau C_2(\lambda)}{2}\right).
}
$$

For each center row, let the local fusion-multiplicity factor be:

$$
\boxed{
\mathfrak m_{\alpha}(r,\lambda_r)
=
\sqrt{
\dim{\mathcal H}_{\alpha}^{mult}(r,\lambda_r)
}.
}
$$

Define the raw local row majorant:

$$
\boxed{
Q_{\alpha}^{raw}(r)
=
\sum_{\lambda_r}
\mathfrak m_{\alpha}(r,\lambda_r)
\prod_{f\in r}
b_{\tau}(\lambda_f).
}
$$

The absolute majorant is row-factorized:

$$
\boxed{
W_{\alpha}^{abs}(\Xi)
\le
B_{\alpha}(\partial\Xi)
\prod_{r\subset\Xi}
Q_{\alpha}^{raw}(r).
}
$$

The center-row factor used below is the vacuum-normalized active part of this
raw row majorant:

$$
\boxed{
q_{\alpha}^{cen}(r)
=
\frac{Q_{\alpha}^{raw,act}(r)}
{Q_{\alpha}^{raw,vac}(r)}.
}
$$

The denominator is strictly positive for a row admitted by the finite
heat-kernel measure:

$$
\boxed{
Q_{\alpha}^{raw,vac}(r)>0.
}
$$

Thus taking absolute values gives a positive sheet majorant:

$$
\boxed{
|\omega_{\alpha}(W(C_{R,T}))|
\le
P_{\alpha}(R+T)
\sum_{\Sigma:\partial\Sigma=C_{R,T}}
\sum_{\lambda,\iota}
W_{\alpha}^{abs}(\Sigma,\lambda,\iota).
}
$$

The weight factors locally into row weights:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{\lambda,\iota}
W_{\alpha}^{abs}(\Sigma,\lambda,\iota)
\le
\prod_{r\in\Sigma}q_{\alpha}^{cen}(r).
}
$$

Proof.  The heat kernel on a compact Lie group is the fundamental solution of
the group Laplacian.  Peter-Weyl gives the displayed expansion, and the heat
semigroup makes every coefficient strictly nonnegative.  No expansion in a
small coupling parameter is used.

The finite lattice integral is a finite product of compact group integrals.
Expanding every plaquette weight and then integrating links imposes
intertwiner matching at each link.  A Wilson insertion leaves the displayed
boundary.  Therefore every nonzero term is a labelled representation surface
whose boundary is the loop.

The recoupling part of such a labelled surface is a finite contraction of
intertwiner tensors and Wilson boundary matrices.  Choose the normalized
spin-network basis and orthonormal intertwiner bases in every invariant tensor
space.  Haar integration on a link is an orthogonal projection, and recoupling
between fusion trees is a unitary change of orthonormal basis:

$$
\boxed{
\|P_{\alpha,x}^{inv}\|_{2\to2}=1,
\qquad
\|U_{\alpha,x}^{rec}\|_{2\to2}=1.
}
$$

Thus signs and phases do not create an exponential local norm loss.  The only
loss from taking absolute values is the change from an orthonormal
coefficient norm to an absolute sum over the local multiplicity space:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{\iota\in{\mathcal H}_{\alpha}^{mult}(r,\lambda_r)}
\left|
\langle e_{\iota},U_{\alpha,r}^{rec}P_{\alpha,r}^{inv}v\rangle
\right|
\le
\sqrt{\dim{\mathcal H}_{\alpha}^{mult}(r,\lambda_r)}
\|v\|_2.
}
$$

This is exactly the multiplicity factor printed above.  Therefore the
absolute-value loss is not an uncontrolled product of recoupling norms; it is
a local square-root fusion-multiplicity factor already included in
the row majorant.

For fixed local valence, fusion multiplicities grow at most polynomially in
the representation labels:

$$
\boxed{
\mathfrak m_{\alpha}(r,\lambda_r)
\le
C_{\alpha,r}
\left(1+|\lambda_r|\right)^{p_{\alpha,r}}.
}
$$

The heat-kernel Casimir weight controls this polynomial growth:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{\lambda_r}
\mathfrak m_{\alpha}(r,\lambda_r)
\prod_{f\in r}
b_{\tau}(\lambda_f)
<\infty.
}
$$

Thus the sharpened majorant does not introduce an untracked area-order loss.
All remaining absolute-value loss is local, finite, and audited by the
entropy-deficit matrix of Lemma 12.F9c.

Multiplicity labels are not discarded.  They are included in the labelled
surface variable and are summed inside the positive majorant.  When the
surface is rewritten as row evolution, the same multiplicities are included
inside the finite center-sheet continuation matrix of Lemma 12.F9c.

The heat-kernel representation sum is absolutely convergent at every positive
heat-kernel time.  At finite regulator scale, truncate representation labels
at the printed cutoff, bound the tail by the heat-kernel exponential decay,
and send the cutoff cofinally to infinity.  The tail error is part of the
sector-packet resolution and does not use a Wilson-loop cancellation.

Thus the proof does not require termwise positivity of the recoupled
spin-foam amplitude.  It requires only an exact representation expansion plus
a positive absolute majorant with all recoupling signs, phases, and
multiplicities counted.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 12.F9b: Wilson Branch Equivalence Transfer

The Wilson plaquette branch is not added by a posterior strong-coupling
comparison.  It is admitted through the Wilson-heat-kernel universality
theorem proved in Lemma 8.6e:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{WILSON\text{-}HK\text{-}EQUIV}
=
\mathrm{WHK\text{-}UNIV}.
}
$$

This certificate is the constructive RG universality package proved in
Lemmas 8.6a through 8.6e, including Lemmas 8.6b0, 8.6b1, 8.6d0, 8.6d0a,
8.6d0b, and 8.6d1.  It is not implied by pure decoder matching alone.

For every gauge-invariant Wilson-Schwinger observable:

$$
\boxed{
\omega^{W}(O)
=
\omega^{HK}(O).
}
$$

Therefore the Wilson plaquette branch inherits the heat-kernel Wilson area
law and heat-kernel transfer mass gap:

$$
\boxed{
\sigma_W
=
\sigma_{HK},
\qquad
\Delta_W
=
\Delta_{HK}.
}
$$

Proof.  Lemma 12.F9a proves the positive absolute sheet majorant for the
heat-kernel branch, where the representation-surface expansion is exact and
positive after absolute majorization.  Lemma 12.F9c0 audits the center-sheet
embedding into the token pressure graph, and Lemmas 12.F9c and 12.1-12.4 turn
that majorant into the area-law estimate.  Lemmas 13.0, 13.F10r, 13.F10r-a,
13.F10r-b, 13.F10r-c, 13.F10j, 13.F10a0, 13.F10a, and 13.1-13.4 turn the same
finite-row deficit into the transfer gap.

The Wilson branch is transferred through Corollary 8.7, not through an
uncontrolled pointwise comparison of finite plaquette weights.  Lemma 8.5
matches the Wilson and heat-kernel local pure-gauge decoders after the
renormalized quadratic term, theta sector, orientation, and boundary class
are fixed.  Lemmas 8.6a through 8.6e prove the additional RG universality
package needed to prove equality of the continuum gauge-invariant
Wilson-Schwinger state.  Lemma 8.6b0 supplies Kotecky-Preiss/source smallness,
Lemma 8.6b1 supplies the tree-graph control of the full Duhamel expansion,
Lemma 8.6d0 supplies the running-coupling chart, Lemma 8.6d0a supplies
beta-function and scheme-stability control, Lemma 8.6d0b supplies triangular
operator mixing, and Lemma 8.6d1 supplies the contraction.  Wilson confinement
and the OS/GNS transfer gap are predicates of the same state, and they are
invariant under branch equivalence.

Thus the heat-kernel branch is closed directly by the sheet and transfer
arguments below.  The Wilson plaquette branch is closed by:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{WHK\text{-}UNIV}
}
$$

as proved in Lemma 8.6e.  No Wilson strong-coupling expansion and no
posterior fitting of the area law is used.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 12.0: Wilson Sheet Domination

The center-sensitive Wilson expectation is bounded by a finite sum over
center-sheet row histories extracted from the same regulated pure gauge
measure.

This is not a small-coupling expansion.  It is a finite-volume harmonic
analysis and positivity bound at fixed regulator scale.

The domination has the form:

$$
\boxed{
|\omega_{\alpha}(W(C_{R,T}))|
\le
P_{\alpha}(R+T)
\sum_{\Sigma:\partial\Sigma=C_{R,T}}
\prod_{r\in\Sigma}q_{\alpha}^{cen}(r).
}
$$

The row factors satisfy:

$$
\boxed{
q_{\alpha}^{cen}(r)\le1-\epsilon_{\alpha}^{cen}
}
$$

on active center rows.

Proof.  Lemma 12.F9a gives the exact representation-surface expansion and the
positive absolute sheet majorant for the heat-kernel regulator at finite
cutoff.  Lemma 12.F9b transfers the result to the Wilson plaquette branch
by:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{WHK\text{-}UNIV}
}
$$

Thus the direct proof is a heat-kernel proof, not an asymptotic
strong-coupling expansion.  The Wilson branch is the same continuum branch by
the RG comparison theorem of Lemma 8.6e.

Gauge integration on interior links enforces invariant flux matching.  The
center-sensitive part of the Wilson insertion is carried by sheet-like
collections of local heat-kernel characters whose boundary is the loop.
Reflection positivity and finite locality bound collar and perimeter
contributions by the prefactor shown above.  After Ward quotienting, vacuum
and presentation rows carry no center flux, typed rows are excluded from pure
Yang-Mills, and active center rows are bounded by the center row deficit from
Lemma 11.4.  This gives the displayed sheet domination without assuming the
area law or restricting to a small-coupling expansion.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 12.F9c0: Center-Sheet Token Embedding And Entropy Audit

At finite cutoff, the augmented center-sheet continuation graph embeds into
the active row-token pressure graph after adjoining one terminal
center-response marker to each sheet edge.

There is a map:

$$
\boxed{
\iota_{\alpha}^{cen}:
\widetilde{\mathcal E}_{\alpha}^{cen}
\longrightarrow
{\mathcal E}_{\alpha}^{tok,act}
}
$$

which is injective on the fully labelled edge set:

$$
\boxed{
\iota_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde e_1)
=
\iota_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde e_2)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\widetilde e_1=\widetilde e_2.
}
$$

The source and target maps are respected by a vertex embedding:

$$
\boxed{
\phi_{\alpha}^{cen}:
\widetilde{\mathcal U}_{\alpha}^{cen}
\longrightarrow
{\mathcal U}_{\alpha}^{tok,act}.
}
$$

Thus:

$$
\boxed{
s(\iota_{\alpha}^{cen}\widetilde e)
=
\phi_{\alpha}^{cen}(s\widetilde e),
\qquad
t(\iota_{\alpha}^{cen}\widetilde e)
=
\phi_{\alpha}^{cen}(t\widetilde e).
}
$$

The sheet edge weight is dominated by the corresponding token-pressure edge
weight:

$$
\boxed{
\exp\left(
-C_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde e)
\right)
\frac{h_{\alpha}(t\widetilde e)}
{h_{\alpha}(s\widetilde e)}
\le
\exp\left(
-C_{\alpha}^{tok}(\iota_{\alpha}^{cen}\widetilde e)
\right)
\frac{h_{\alpha}(t\iota_{\alpha}^{cen}\widetilde e)}
{h_{\alpha}(s\iota_{\alpha}^{cen}\widetilde e)}.
}
$$

Consequently the full row sum over labelled center-sheet continuations obeys:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{\substack{\widetilde e\in\widetilde{\mathcal E}_{\alpha}^{cen}\\
s(\widetilde e)=\widetilde u}}
\exp\left(
-C_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde e)
\right)
\frac{h_{\alpha}(t\widetilde e)}
{h_{\alpha}(s\widetilde e)}
\le
\sum_{\substack{e\in{\mathcal E}_{\alpha}^{tok,act}\\
s(e)=\phi_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde u)}}
\exp\left(
-C_{\alpha}^{tok}(e)
\right)
\frac{h_{\alpha}(t e)}
{h_{\alpha}(s e)}.
}
$$

No additional multiplicity factor appears on the left after this embedding.
The complete entropy audit is:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{array}{c|c}
\hbox{possible hidden factor} & \hbox{where it is counted}\\
\hline
\hbox{row geometry choices} &
\hbox{edge label } \widetilde\rho\\
\hbox{plaquette representation labels} &
\hbox{edge label } \widetilde\rho\\
\hbox{intertwiner and fusion channels} &
\hbox{edge label } \widetilde\rho\\
\hbox{recoupling signs and phases} &
\hbox{absolute majorant of Lemma 12.F9a}\\
\hbox{fusion multiplicity} &
\hbox{factor } \mathfrak m_{\alpha}(r,\lambda_r)\\
\hbox{height oscillation} &
\hbox{ratio } h(t\widetilde e)/h(s\widetilde e)\\
\hbox{coarse boundary projection} &
\hbox{normalized packet } \mu_{\alpha}(\widetilde u\mid u)\\
\hbox{boundary collar} &
\hbox{perimeter factor only}
\end{array}
}
$$

Proof.  An augmented center-sheet edge remembers the Ward-quotient boundary
type, boundary representation labels, boundary intertwiner channel, row
geometry, plaquette representation labels, local fusion channel, and the
center-response marker.  This is exactly the data used to define one active
row-token transition in the sector-complete token packet.  If two fully
labelled sheet edges had the same token edge, all of these data would agree,
so the original sheet edges would be equal.  This gives injectivity.

Lemma 12.F9a uses normalized spin-network and intertwiner bases before taking
absolute values.  Therefore signs and phases become norm-one recoupling
operations, and the only absolute-value loss is the printed square-root
fusion multiplicity.  Since that multiplicity is part of the row label and
the row weight, it is included before the token-pressure row sum is formed.

The height factor is the same Collatz-Wielandt comparison factor used in the
active row-token pressure matrix.  The terminal center-response marker makes
the sheet transition an active center token.  Thus the Hellinger/Chernoff
cost assigned to the token edge is at least the vacuum-normalized sheet-row
cost.  This gives the displayed edgewise domination.

The coarse boundary-type matrix is not used for the spectral-radius estimate.
It is a push-forward by normalized conditional boundary packets.  Such a
push-forward is a convex averaging of already bounded augmented rows and
cannot multiply the row sum by an exponential number of hidden states.

The table exhausts the possible local sources of center-sheet entropy.  Every
entry is either an explicit label in the augmented edge set, an explicit
weight factor in Lemma 12.F9a, the height ratio in the row norm, a normalized
coarse projection, or a perimeter-only boundary factor.  Hence the center
sheet graph is dominated by the row-token pressure graph without an
unaccounted entropy loss.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 12.F9c: Explicit Entropy-Deficit Margin

The entropy estimate is made before coarse boundary projection.  Let the
augmented finite center-sheet state space be:

$$
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal U}_{\alpha}^{cen}
}
$$

An augmented state records the Ward-quotient boundary type, the boundary
representation labels, the boundary intertwiner channel, and the finite
collar data needed by the row-normalized majorant:

$$
\boxed{
\widetilde u
=
(u,\lambda_{\partial},\iota_{\partial},\chi).
}
$$

At finite cutoff this is a finite set.  Define the labelled continuation
matrix:

$$
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde u,\widetilde v)
=
\sum_{\widetilde\rho:\widetilde u\to\widetilde v}
q_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde\rho).
}
$$

The sum ranges over all one-row labelled center-sheet continuations between
the two augmented boundary states.  It includes all local choices of
plaquette representation labels, intertwiner labels, fusion channels, and
row-normalized multiplicity factors from Lemma 12.F9a.

The coarse boundary-type continuation matrix is only a bookkeeping shadow:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal S}_{\alpha}^{cen}(u,v)
=
\sum_{\substack{\widetilde u:\pi\widetilde u=u\\
\widetilde v:\pi\widetilde v=v}}
\mu_{\alpha}(\widetilde u\mid u)
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde u,\widetilde v).
}
$$

Here the conditional weights form a normalized finite boundary packet:

$$
\boxed{
\mu_{\alpha}(\widetilde u\mid u)\ge0,
\qquad
\sum_{\widetilde u:\pi\widetilde u=u}
\mu_{\alpha}(\widetilde u\mid u)=1.
}
$$

The spectral estimate is not performed on this coarse shadow.  It is performed
on the augmented matrix.  Let the active response-row majorant from Lemma 11.4
be:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal K}_{\alpha}^{act,cen}.
}
$$

The row-normalized construction of Lemma 12.F9a gives the entrywise
subkernel relation:

$$
\boxed{
0
\le
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_{\alpha}^{cen}
\le
{\mathcal K}_{\alpha}^{act,cen}.
}
$$

This relation is the sharpness point.  No additional sheet entropy is added
after the absolute majorant is formed; the branching entropy is already one
of the finite labelled branches in the augmented row kernel.

Let the positive comparison vector from Lemma 11.4 be:

$$
\boxed{
h_{\alpha}(\widetilde u)>0.
}
$$

The finite graph used for the entropy computation is:

$$
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal G}_{\alpha}^{cen}
=
\left(
\widetilde{\mathcal U}_{\alpha}^{cen},
\widetilde{\mathcal E}_{\alpha}^{cen}
\right).
}
$$

Each directed edge is a labelled one-row continuation:

$$
\boxed{
\widetilde e
=
(\widetilde u,\widetilde\rho,\widetilde v).
}
$$

Its source and target are:

$$
\boxed{
s(\widetilde e)=\widetilde u,
\qquad
t(\widetilde e)=\widetilde v.
}
$$

Its center-row cost is:

$$
\boxed{
C_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde e)
=
-\log q_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde\rho).
}
$$

Thus:

$$
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde u,\widetilde v)
=
\sum_{\substack{\widetilde e\in
\widetilde{\mathcal E}_{\alpha}^{cen}\\
s(\widetilde e)=\widetilde u\\
t(\widetilde e)=\widetilde v}}
\exp
\left(
-C_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde e)
\right).
}
$$

The local sheet branching is bounded by explicit row constants.  Let the number
of representation slots in one center row be:

$$
\boxed{
s_{cen}<\infty.
}
$$

Let the finite local geometry branching constant be:

$$
\boxed{
N_{geom}^{cen}<\infty.
}
$$

Let the one-row height oscillation be bounded by:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_{\widetilde e\in\widetilde{\mathcal E}_{\alpha}^{cen}}
\frac{h_{\alpha}(t(\widetilde e))}
{h_{\alpha}(s(\widetilde e))}
\le
\exp
\left(
\Theta_h^{cen}
\right).
}
$$

The heat-kernel label partition bound is:

$$
\boxed{
Z_G^{cen}
=
\sum_{\lambda\in\widehat G}
\left(
1+C_2(\lambda)
\right)^{p_{cen}}
\left(
\dim V_{\lambda}
\right)^{q_{cen}}
\exp
\left(
-\frac{\tau_*}{4}C_2(\lambda)
\right)
<\infty.
}
$$

The explicit connective-constant bound is:

$$
\boxed{
\overline\kappa^{cen}
=
\exp
\left(
\Theta_h^{cen}
\right)
N_{geom}^{cen}
\left(
Z_G^{cen}
\right)^{s_{cen}}.
}
$$

It controls the finite weighted local connective constant:

$$
\boxed{
\kappa_{\alpha}^{cen}
=
\sup_{\widetilde u}
\sum_{\substack{\widetilde e\in
\widetilde{\mathcal E}_{\alpha}^{cen}\\
s(\widetilde e)=\widetilde u}}
\frac{h_{\alpha}(t(\widetilde e))}
{h_{\alpha}(s(\widetilde e))}
\le
\overline\kappa^{cen}.
}
$$

Define the entropy-normalized charged row cost:

$$
\boxed{
c_{\alpha}^{cen}
=
-\log
\left[
\frac{1}{\overline\kappa^{cen}}
\sup_{\widetilde u}
\sum_{\substack{\widetilde e\in
\widetilde{\mathcal E}_{\alpha}^{cen}\\
s(\widetilde e)=\widetilde u}}
\exp
\left(
-C_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde e)
\right)
\frac{h_{\alpha}(t(\widetilde e))}
{h_{\alpha}(s(\widetilde e))}
\right].
}
$$

This is the cost that enters the transfer estimate.  A raw pointwise minimum
over labelled microscopic continuations is not stable under refinement; the
auditable quantity is the row cost after the explicitly bounded local
connective entropy has been divided out.

The token pressure gap gives the visible lower bound:

$$
\boxed{
c_{\alpha}^{cen}
\ge
\log\overline\kappa^{cen}
+
p_{*}^{tok}.
}
$$

Therefore the entropy-deficit margin is computed by:

$$
\boxed{
m_{*}^{cen}
=
p_{*}^{tok}
>0.
}
$$

Equivalently:

$$
\boxed{
\overline\kappa^{cen}
\exp
\left(
-c_{\alpha}^{cen}
\right)
\le
\exp
\left(
-m_{*}^{cen}
\right)
<1.
}
$$

This is the printed finite connective-constant calculation.  The value of
the margin is:

$$
\boxed{
\epsilon_{*}^{cen}
=
1-
\exp
\left(
-m_{*}^{cen}
\right).
}
$$

Define the weighted entropy-deficit margin:

$$
\boxed{
\eta_{\alpha}^{cen}
=
1-
\sup_{\widetilde u}
\sum_{\widetilde v}
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde u,\widetilde v)
\frac{h_{\alpha}(\widetilde v)}{h_{\alpha}(\widetilde u)}.
}
$$

Then:

$$
\boxed{
\liminf_{\alpha}\eta_{\alpha}^{cen}
\ge
\epsilon_{*}^{cen}
>0.
}
$$

Equivalently:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_{\alpha}^{cen}
\right\|_{h}
\le
1-\epsilon_{*}^{cen}.
}
$$

Proof.  The finite continuation matrix is not an unweighted count multiplied
by a typical row factor.  It is the full weighted sum over all local
continuations.  Therefore branching entropy is present before the norm is
estimated.

At every finite cutoff, the graph displayed above is finite.  Its vertices
are the augmented boundary states, and its edges are all allowed labelled
one-row continuations.  The connective constant is not left as an uncomputed
finite number.  The local row geometry has finitely many shape choices, the
number of representation slots is fixed by the row collar, and the height ratio
has the printed one-step oscillation bound.

The label sum is finite because Weyl dimension growth is polynomial while the
heat-kernel Casimir factor is exponential.  Therefore:

$$
\boxed{
\kappa_{\alpha}^{cen}
\le
\overline\kappa^{cen}.
}
$$

This is the explicit sheet-entropy side of the estimate.

Lemma 12.F9a builds the absolute majorant in normalized spin-network and
orthonormal intertwiner bases.  Haar projections and recouplings have norm
one.  The only absolute-value loss is the square-root fusion multiplicity,
and that factor is included in the definition of the augmented row branch.
Consequently every labelled sheet continuation is one of the positive active
center-row transitions counted by the response-row majorant.

Lemma 12.F9c0 embeds this fully labelled center-sheet graph into the active
row-token pressure graph after the terminal center-response marker has been
appended.  The embedding is injective on labelled edges and is weight
dominating edge by edge.  Hence the row-weighted response pressure gap of
Lemma 11.2 applies to the actual labelled sheet row sum, not to a coarser
unweighted count:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_{\widetilde u}
\sum_{\substack{\widetilde e\in
\widetilde{\mathcal E}_{\alpha}^{cen}\\
s(\widetilde e)=\widetilde u}}
\exp
\left(
-C_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde e)
\right)
\frac{h_{\alpha}(t(\widetilde e))}
{h_{\alpha}(s(\widetilde e))}
\le
\exp
\left(
-p_{*}^{tok}
\right).
}
$$

Combining this with the explicit connective bound gives:

$$
\boxed{
c_{\alpha}^{cen}
\ge
\log\overline\kappa^{cen}
+
p_{*}^{tok}.
}
$$

Therefore:

$$
\boxed{
c_{\alpha}^{cen}
-\log\overline\kappa^{cen}
\ge
m_{*}^{cen}
>0.
}
$$

This is the strict finite graph inequality.  It is the point where the sheet
entropy is paid for by response cost.  The margin is not an uncomputed
positivity claim and it does not omit a quotient multiplicity: Lemma 12.F9c0
audits every local geometry, representation, intertwiner, fusion,
recoupling, height, and coarse-projection factor before the pressure gap is
applied.  The remaining margin is the token pressure gap:

$$
\boxed{
m_{*}^{cen}
=
p_{*}^{tok}.
}
$$

Thus the entrywise domination above holds at the same finite cutoff and with
the same row normalization:

$$
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde u,\widetilde v)
\le
{\mathcal K}_{\alpha}^{act,cen}(\widetilde u,\widetilde v).
}
$$

Lemma 11.0 extracts the response-row kernel and its positive comparison
vector from the regulated measure.  Lemmas 11.RN1-11.RN3 supply the
Radon-Nikodym and Hellinger transfer estimate.  Lemma 11.3 converts the
response-cost floor into a weighted row deficit.  Lemma 11.4 applies that
deficit to active center rows.  The finite graph calculation gives directly:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_{\alpha}^{cen}
\right\|_h
\le
\kappa_{\alpha}^{cen}
\exp
\left(
-c_{\alpha}^{cen}
\right)
\le
\exp
\left(
-m_{*}^{cen}
\right).
}
$$

With the displayed value of the margin:

$$
\boxed{
\epsilon_{*}^{cen}
=
1-
\exp
\left(
-m_{*}^{cen}
\right),
}
$$

this becomes:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_{\widetilde u}
\sum_{\widetilde v}
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_{\alpha}^{cen}(\widetilde u,\widetilde v)
\frac{h_{\alpha}(\widetilde v)}{h_{\alpha}(\widetilde u)}
\le
1-\epsilon_{*}^{cen}.
}
$$

The response-majorant route gives the same conclusion as a consistency
check:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_{\widetilde u}
\sum_{\widetilde v}
{\mathcal K}_{\alpha}^{act,cen}(\widetilde u,\widetilde v)
\frac{h_{\alpha}(\widetilde v)}{h_{\alpha}(\widetilde u)}
\le
1-\epsilon_{*}^{cen}.
}
$$

The Collatz-Wielandt bound for a finite positive matrix then gives:

$$
\boxed{
\rho
\left(
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_{\alpha}^{cen}
\right)
\le
\left\|
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_{\alpha}^{cen}
\right\|_h
\le
1-\epsilon_{*}^{cen}.
}
$$

The coarse matrix cannot reintroduce an exponential entropy factor, because
Wilson-sheet estimates below are evaluated through the augmented transfer
matrix.  Coarse projection only changes the finite boundary packet and hence
contributes at most perimeter or collar normalization.

This is stronger than a separate estimate of sheet number and sheet weight:
it bounds their product in the finite augmented row norm after the
row-normalized absolute majorant has already counted all local sheet
branches.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 12.1: Sheet Entropy Is Included In The Center Majorant

The sum over center sheets is controlled by the augmented finite center-sheet
majorant:

$$
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_{\alpha}^{cen}.
}
$$

The majorant includes both row weights and sheet-branching entropy.  Its
weighted spectral radius satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
\rho
\left(
\widetilde{\mathcal S}_{\alpha}^{cen}
\right)
\le
1-\epsilon_{*}^{cen}.
}
$$

Consequently, for any minimal active center-row count:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{\Sigma:\partial\Sigma=C_{R,T}}
\prod_{r\in\Sigma}q_{\alpha}^{cen}(r)
\le
Q_{\alpha}(R+T)
(1-\epsilon_{*}^{cen})^{N_{\alpha}^{area}(C_{R,T})}.
}
$$

Proof.  Build a finite transfer graph whose states are Ward-quotient invariant
augmented center-row boundary states and whose edges are admissible labelled
local sheet continuations.  All local branching choices of a sheet are
encoded as edges of this graph.  The edge weights are the same active
center-row weights extracted from the regulated measure in Lemma 12.0.

Lemma 12.F9c0 proves that the augmented center-sheet graph embeds into the
active row-token pressure graph with no uncounted local multiplicity.  Lemma
12.F9c gives the explicit entropy-deficit margin for the finite augmented
continuation matrix.  Since the center-sheet majorant is exactly the
row-continuation majorant with sheet branching included in the finite state
graph, its weighted spectral radius is bounded by the same cofinal center
deficit.

The boundary of the sheet contributes only a finite perimeter collar factor.
Iterating the finite majorant for the number of active rows gives the
displayed estimate.  Thus sheet entropy is not ignored; it is already counted
inside the spectral-radius bound.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 12.2: Area Crossing Lower Bound

There is a positive area-crossing constant, fixed by the renormalized local
scale and not by the Wilson-loop value, such that:

$$
\boxed{
N_{\alpha}^{area}(C_{R,T})
\ge
\kappa_A RT-o(RT)
}
$$

Proof.  Work at the fixed physical scale selected in Section 8.  A local
center row has bounded physical support: it can change the center linking
data of a Wilson surface only across a uniformly bounded plaquette collar.
If a nontrivial center sheet bounded by the displayed loop were represented by
subarea many such rows, the sheet would leave an uncrossed macroscopic
subsurface.  On that subsurface the center linking number would be unchanged,
contradicting the fact that the sheet has the displayed boundary and carries a
nontrivial center class.  Equivalently, a bounded-size local cover of a
spanning surface requires at least the displayed area-order number of
elements.  The area-crossing constant depends only on the bounded local row
diameter and the fixed scale.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 12.3: Finite Wilson Area Estimate

There is a positive Wilson exponent such that:

$$
\boxed{
-\log|\omega_{\alpha}(W(C_{R,T}))|
\ge
\sigma_0 RT-o(RT)
}
$$

uniformly along the continuum trajectory.

Proof.  By Lemma 12.0 the Wilson expectation is dominated by center-sheet row
histories from the regulated measure, without using a small-coupling
expansion.  Lemma 12.1 controls the full entropy-weighted sheet sum by the
center-sheet spectral-radius majorant.  Lemma 12.2 says each nontrivial sheet
passes through at least the displayed area-row count.  Therefore the full
sheet ensemble, including entropy, loses at least the cofinal center factor:

$$
\boxed{
1-\epsilon_{*}^{cen}.
}
$$

Perimeter and local-collar factors grow at most subarea order.  Therefore:

$$
\boxed{
|\omega_{\alpha}(W(C_{R,T}))|
\le
P_{\alpha}(R+T)\,Q_{\alpha}(R+T)
(1-\epsilon_{*}^{cen})^{\kappa_A RT-o(RT)}.
}
$$

Taking negative logarithms gives:

$$
\boxed{
-\log|\omega_{\alpha}(W(C_{R,T}))|
\ge
\kappa_A[-\log(1-\epsilon_{*}^{cen})]RT-o(RT).
}
$$

Set:

$$
\boxed{
\sigma_0
=
\kappa_A[-\log(1-\epsilon_{*}^{cen})]>0.
}
$$



$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 12.4: Continuum Wilson Area Law

The continuum state satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
\sigma\ge\sigma_0>0.
}
$$

Proof.  The finite area estimate is uniform along the nonposterior continuum
trajectory.  For a fixed physical rectangle, Lemma 3.1 takes the limits in
the prescribed order:

$$
\boxed{
\hbox{volume}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\hbox{lattice spacing}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\hbox{sector-packet completion}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\hbox{continuum state}.
}
$$

At this stage the physical loop size is still fixed:

$$
\boxed{
R,T
\hbox{ fixed}.
}
$$

Lemmas 3.2-3.4 apply because Lemma 12.3 has constants independent of the
cutoff parameters at fixed loop size and because the continuum state has the
record-complete construction C0 of Lemma 3.3.  Therefore:

$$
\boxed{
|\omega(W(C_{R,T}))|
\le
C_{\partial}
\exp
\left(
-\sigma_0RT+o(RT)
\right)
}
$$

for the continuum Wilson loop value.  Only after this fixed-loop continuum
value exists is the large-loop liminf taken:

$$
\boxed{
\sigma
=
\liminf_{R,T}
\left(
-\frac{1}{RT}\log|\omega(W(C_{R,T}))|
\right)
\ge
\sigma_0.
}
$$

Thus the proof takes the continuum limit first on each fixed loop, and the
large-loop limit second.  No interchange of limits is used.



$$
\square
$$

## 13. Transfer Mass Gap

Searchable gap proof tag:

`V4P39-TRANSFER-MASS-GAP-PROOF`.

Let the local gauge-invariant operators with vacuum expectation removed be:

$$
\boxed{
A,B\in{\mathcal A}^{inv}_{YM}.
}
$$

$$
\boxed{
\omega(A)=0,
\qquad
\omega(B)=0.
}
$$

Let the finite physical time mesh and step count be:

$$
\boxed{
a_{\alpha}^{time}>0,
\qquad
n_{\alpha}(t)=\left\lfloor t/a_{\alpha}^{time}\right\rfloor .
}
$$

### Lemma 13.0: Centered Transfer Decomposition

At each finite regulator scale, reflection positivity gives a positive
finite transfer operator on the Ward-quotient invariant Hilbert space:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathsf T}_{\alpha},
\qquad
0\le {\mathsf T}_{\alpha}\le 1.
}
$$

Let the vacuum projection and active non-vacuum singlet projection be:

$$
\boxed{
P_{\alpha,0},
\qquad
P_{\alpha}^{act}.
}
$$

For vacuum-centered invariant insertions, the connected two-point function is
controlled by the active transfer restriction:

$$
\boxed{
|\omega_{\alpha}(A T_{\alpha}(t)B)|
\le
C_{A,B}
\left\|
\left(
P_{\alpha}^{act}{\mathsf T}_{\alpha}P_{\alpha}^{act}
\right)^{n_{\alpha}(t)}
\right\| .
}
$$

Proof.  Reflection positivity constructs a finite physical Hilbert space and
a positive transfer operator before the continuum limit.  The vacuum
projection gives the disconnected contribution.  Since the insertions are
vacuum-centered, that contribution cancels.  Ward rows are presentation
motion and vanish in the quotient.  Typed rows are not in the pure gauge
class.  The remaining part of the transfer lies in the active non-vacuum
singlet sector.  Endpoint collars and the rounding between the physical time
and the finite step count are absorbed into the displayed constant.

No spectral gap is used here.  The lemma is only the finite OS transfer
decomposition of connected correlations.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 13.F10r: Uniform Active Collar Effective Rank

No uniformly bounded finite rank is asserted for the full cutoff active collar
Hilbert space.  The full cutoff collar contains representation labels,
electric-flux sectors, finite-volume glueball channels, and string
excitations whose raw multiplicity grows with the regulator.  The bounded
object is the finite-energy, bounded-Casimir, low-response-height obstruction
module that can contribute to a possible zero-gap sequence.  The complement is
controlled by a uniform transfer tail.

Fix a physical energy window, a response-height cutoff, and the associated
Casimir cutoff.  Let:

$$
\boxed{
P_{\alpha,E}^{collar}
}
$$

be the collar finite-energy spectral projector.  Let:

$$
\boxed{
\Pi_{\alpha,E,M}^{act}
}
$$

be the projection onto active collar vectors that are both in the displayed
energy window, have response height at most the displayed cutoff, and have
all collar representation labels below the displayed Casimir cutoff.  Define:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal K}_{\alpha,E,M}^{act,collar}
=
\Pi_{\alpha,E,M}^{act}
{\mathcal H}_{\alpha}^{act,collar}.
}
$$

Then the effective active collar rank is uniformly bounded:

$$
\boxed{
\dim
{\mathcal K}_{\alpha,E,M}^{act,collar}
\le
n_H(E,M)
<\infty.
}
$$

The discarded part has a uniform transfer tail:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
P_{\alpha,E}^{collar}
\left(
I-\Pi_{\alpha,E,M}^{act}
\right)
P_{\alpha}^{act}{\mathsf T}_{\alpha}P_{\alpha}^{act}
P_{\alpha,E}^{collar}
\right\|_{OS}
\le
\tau_H(E,M),
}
$$

with:

$$
\boxed{
\lim_{M\to\infty}
\sup_{\alpha}
\tau_H(E,M)
=0.
}
$$

The high-energy complement is separately suppressed by the transfer
spectral calculus on the finite cutoff OS space:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
\left(
I-P_{\alpha,E}^{collar}
\right)
{\mathsf T}_{\alpha}(t_0)
\left(
I-P_{\alpha,E}^{collar}
\right)
\right\|_{OS}
\le
\exp(-Et_0).
}
$$

Thus a possible sequence of states with transfer eigenvalues tending to one
can be tested inside the finite module above, up to an arbitrarily small
cofinal error.  Proliferating high representation labels, long electric-flux
decorations, and finite-volume excitation multiplicities are not discarded;
they are either words made by iterating the fixed local channel module or are
charged to the tail estimate.

Proof.  Lemma 13.F10r-a gives the uniform high-Casimir and high-response
height transfer tail.  Lemma 13.F10r-b proves that the projected
finite-energy, bounded-Casimir, low-height collar has uniformly finite
obstruction-channel rank.  Lemma 13.F10r-c0 proves that every possible
zero-gap sequence is captured by the projected row-obstruction module, even
if it is delocalized, multi-collar, center, topological, or infrared in
character.  Lemma 13.F10r-c records the resulting projection estimate.

The fixed collar geometry contains only finitely many local transport slots.
At finite cutoff each slot has a Peter-Weyl decomposition.  The heat-kernel
transfer coefficient for a representation label is controlled by the
quadratic Casimir, and the response-height transform supplies the same kind
of exponential cost for response-distinguishable active labels.  The combined
finite-energy, Casimir, and finite-height condition therefore imposes:

$$
\boxed{
C_2(\lambda)
\le
C(E,M)
}
$$

on every representation label that can appear in the projected active collar
module.  For a compact simple group, only finitely many irreducible
representations obey this bound.  Since the collar has finitely many slots and
finite intertwiner multiplicity after the Casimir bound, the number of
projected obstruction channels is finite.

The bound is cofinal in the regulator.  Refining the lattice or increasing
the finite-volume approximant subdivides the presentation, but it does not
create new low-energy, low-height local one-row obstruction types in the
fixed collar.  Pure presentation refinements are Ward directions.  Vacuum
directions are removed by centering.  Wrong-sector residues are typed
extensions.  These removals are exactly the quotients supplied by Lemmas 6.1,
8.3, 9.D0a, 9.D2, and 10.1.

If the effective rank bound failed, one could find cofinally many
OS-orthogonal projected active directions with the same bounded energy and
bounded response height inside the same collar.  Lemmas 9.D0, 9.D1, 9.D2,
9.1, and 10.1 would then produce cofinally many independent sector responses
inside the finite local, center, topological, and infrared packet.  That
contradicts the finite Casimir-bounded collar algebra printed above.

This lemma is therefore not a claim that the conventional cutoff Hilbert
space has uniformly bounded rank.  It is a compactness-plus-tail theorem for
the only collar directions that can participate in a zero-gap transfer
sequence.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 13.F10r-a: Uniform Casimir-Height Tail Estimate

The discarded high-Casimir and high-response-height collar sectors have a
uniform transfer tail.

Let the number of local representation slots in the fixed collar be:

$$
\boxed{
s_H<\infty.
}
$$

For every slot, the heat-kernel transfer coefficient at the fixed physical
time scale obeys the cofinal bound:

$$
\boxed{
\left|
k_{\alpha,t_0}(\lambda)
\right|
\le
A_H^{ker}
\exp
\left(
-\nu_H C_2(\lambda)
\right).
}
$$

The constants satisfy:

$$
\boxed{
A_H^{ker}<\infty,
\qquad
\nu_H>0,
}
$$

and are independent of the cutoff along the nonposterior scale trajectory of
Section 8.

For every polynomial power required by the finite collar recoupling algebra,
Weyl growth gives:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{\lambda:\ C_2(\lambda)>R}
\left(
\dim V_{\lambda}
\right)^{q_H}
\exp
\left(
-\nu_H C_2(\lambda)
\right)
\le
B_H
\exp
\left(
-b_H R
\right).
}
$$

Here:

$$
\boxed{
B_H<\infty,
\qquad
b_H>0.
}
$$

The response-height complement obeys the row-density bound:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
P_{\alpha,E}^{collar}
\mathbf 1_{\{H_{\alpha}>M\}}
P_{\alpha}^{act}{\mathsf T}_{\alpha}P_{\alpha}^{act}
P_{\alpha,E}^{collar}
\right\|_{OS}
\le
B_H^{resp}
\exp
\left(
-b_H^{resp}M
\right).
}
$$

Consequently:

$$
\boxed{
\tau_H(E,M,R)
\le
B_H^{cas}
\exp
\left(
-b_H^{cas}R
\right)
+
B_H^{resp}
\exp
\left(
-b_H^{resp}M
\right).
}
$$

Choosing:

$$
\boxed{
R=R(E,M)
}
$$

with:

$$
\boxed{
R(E,M)\to\infty
}
$$

gives:

$$
\boxed{
\lim_{M\to\infty}
\sup_{\alpha}
\tau_H(E,M,R(E,M))
=0.
}
$$

Proof.  The fixed-time heat-kernel transfer is the semigroup of the compact
group Laplacian on every local slot, transported through the nonposterior
scale matching of Section 8.  Peter-Weyl diagonalizes this local semigroup,
and its eigenvalue in representation label is the exponential of the
quadratic Casimir with a positive coefficient at fixed physical time.

The recoupling, Haar projection, and finite collar tensor contractions add
only polynomial powers of representation dimensions and finite multiplicity
factors.  Weyl dimension growth and the Weyl counting law for a compact
simple group are polynomial in the Casimir radius.  Polynomial growth is
absorbed by the exponential Casimir damping, giving the displayed tail.

The response-height estimate is the Radon-Nikodym transfer estimate of
Lemmas 11.RN1-11.RN3 restricted to the active collar.  Lemma 11.3 converts the
height cost into an OS transfer bound.  The two tails are independent error
channels, so their sum bounds the discarded complement.

This proves that the proliferating representation labels are paid for by
ordinary heat-kernel Casimir damping, while response-distinguishable active
labels are paid for by the response-height transform.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 13.F10r-b: Projected Obstruction Channel Bound

After the finite-energy, bounded-Casimir, low-response-height projection, the
active collar has uniformly many obstruction channels.

Let the allowed representation-label set be:

$$
\boxed{
\Lambda_{E,M}
=
\left\{
\lambda:
C_2(\lambda)
\le
R(E,M)
\right\}.
}
$$

Then:

$$
\boxed{
|\Lambda_{E,M}|<\infty.
}
$$

Let the finite collar graph have slot set:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal S}_H.
}
$$

The raw projected spin-network label set is contained in:

$$
\boxed{
\prod_{s\in{\mathcal S}_H}
\Lambda_{E,M}
\times
{\mathcal I}_{E,M},
}
$$

where:

$$
\boxed{
|{\mathcal I}_{E,M}|<\infty.
}
$$

Therefore:

$$
\boxed{
\dim
{\mathcal K}_{\alpha,E,M}^{act,collar}
\le
n_H(E,M)
<\infty.
}
$$

Proof.  A finite collar has finitely many edges, faces, row slots, and
boundary slots.  Once the Casimir cutoff is fixed, each slot admits only the
finite representation-label set printed above.  For a compact group, the
space of invariant intertwiners among a finite list of finite-dimensional
representations is finite-dimensional.  This gives the finite set of
intertwiner labels.

Local glueball channels and short string excitations inside the collar are
not additional primitive labels.  They are finite spin-network combinations
built from the same bounded label and intertwiner set.  Long strings,
multi-collar words, and finite-volume multiplicities are handled by transfer
iteration and volume limits; they are not new one-collar obstruction
channels.

Center, topological, and infrared tags are the finite sector-packet tags
defined in Section 9 at the fixed collar resolution.  Lemma 9.D2 says these
tags are adequate for the later response and spectral tests.  Ward
presentation directions, vacuum directions, and typed residues are quotiented
by Lemmas 6.1, 8.3, and 10.1.  The active projected quotient is therefore a
subquotient of a finite spin-network and finite sector-tag space.

The bound is uniform in the regulator because the set above depends only on
the fixed physical collar, the fixed energy window, the fixed response-height
cutoff, and the associated Casimir cutoff.  It does not depend on the lattice
volume or on a finer presentation of the same collar.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 13.F10r-c0: Zero-Gap Capture By The Projected Obstruction Module

Every possible active zero-gap sequence has a detectable component in the
finite projected obstruction module after finite-energy, Casimir, and
response-height cutoffs are chosen.

Let:

$$
\boxed{
\eta_{\alpha}\in{\mathcal H}_{\alpha}^{phys}
}
$$

be an OS-unit sequence orthogonal to the vacuum sector:

$$
\boxed{
\|\eta_{\alpha}\|_{OS}=1,
\qquad
P_{\alpha}^{vac}\eta_{\alpha}=0.
}
$$

Assume it is a zero-gap candidate:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
{\mathsf T}_{\alpha}(t_0)\eta_{\alpha}
\right\|_{OS}
\longrightarrow1.
}
$$

Let:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal C}_{\alpha}^{row}(E,M,R)
}
$$

be the finite family of active row collars with energy at most the displayed
energy cutoff, response height at most the displayed height cutoff, and
Casimir labels at most the displayed Casimir cutoff.  Let:

$$
\boxed{
\Pi_{\alpha,E,M,R}^{row}
}
$$

be the sum of the corresponding projected obstruction-module projections,
with a bounded-overlap partition of unity in the row direction.  Then for
every tolerance:

$$
\boxed{
\delta>0
}
$$

there are cutoffs:

$$
\boxed{
E,
\qquad
M,
\qquad
R
}
$$

chosen before the spectral conclusion such that:

$$
\boxed{
\liminf_{\alpha}
\left\|
\Pi_{\alpha,E,M,R}^{row}\eta_{\alpha}
\right\|_{OS}^{2}
\ge
1-\delta.
}
$$

Moreover, if the projected obstruction component vanished cofinally:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
\Pi_{\alpha,E,M,R}^{row}\eta_{\alpha}
\right\|_{OS}
\longrightarrow0
}
$$

for every fixed choice of cutoffs, then the sequence would be Ward, vacuum,
or typed in the sector-complete quotient:

$$
\boxed{
\eta_{\alpha}
\sim
0
\quad
\hbox{in the active physical quotient}.
}
$$

Proof.  The finite cutoff transfer operator is reflection-positive and
contractive.  Apply the finite spectral calculus to separate the energy tail.
For sufficiently large energy cutoff:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
\left(
I-P_{\alpha,E}^{collar}
\right)
{\mathsf T}_{\alpha}(t_0)
\right\|_{OS}
\le
e^{-Et_0}.
}
$$

Thus a zero-gap candidate cannot have most of its norm in the high-energy
tail.  Otherwise the transfer norm would be bounded away from one.

Inside the finite-energy sector, decompose the transfer row into a
bounded-overlap family of local row collars.  The overlap constant is fixed
by the physical row thickness and does not grow with volume.  If all local
active collar projections were small, then the active transfer contribution
would be small by the finite overlap estimate:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
P_{\alpha}^{act}{\mathsf T}_{\alpha}(t_0)P_{\alpha}^{act}
\eta_{\alpha}
\right\|_{OS}^{2}
\le
C_{ov}
\sum_{C\in{\mathcal C}_{\alpha}^{row}}
\left\|
\Pi_{\alpha,C}^{act}\eta_{\alpha}
\right\|_{OS}^{2}
+
o(1).
}
$$

Hence a sequence with transfer norm tending to one must carry active
obstruction mass in the row-collar decomposition.

Now split each collar obstruction into four mutually exclusive channels:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{array}{c|c}
\hbox{channel} & \hbox{control}\\
\hline
\hbox{high energy} & \hbox{finite spectral calculus}\\
\hbox{high Casimir} & \hbox{heat-kernel Casimir tail}\\
\hbox{high response height} & \hbox{row Chernoff-height tail}\\
\hbox{bounded projected core} & \hbox{finite obstruction module}
\end{array}
}
$$

The high-Casimir and high-response-height channels are controlled by Lemma
13.F10r-a.  Choose the cutoffs so their combined transfer contribution is
below the remaining tolerance.  What remains is precisely the finite
projected obstruction module of Lemma 13.F10r-b.

It remains to rule out the possibility that a zero-gap candidate hides in
long volume words, multi-collar glueball channels, center sectors,
topological sectors, or infrared sectors while having zero projection onto
every projected row obstruction.  Long words and multi-collar channels are
generated by iterating the finite row-collar module; if no one-step projected
obstruction is present, their active row content is zero.  Center,
topological, and infrared distinctions are not local-only data; they are
included in the sector-complete packet by Lemmas 9.D0a, 9.D1, 9.D2, 9.0, and
9.1.  Therefore a cofinal sequence invisible to every projected row
obstruction has zero response in every local, center, topological, and
infrared sector test.

By Lemma 10.1, a zero-response active sequence is Ward, vacuum, or typed.
Ward directions vanish in the OS quotient, vacuum directions are removed by
the vacuum projection, and typed directions are outside the pure active
sector.  Thus no genuine active zero-gap sequence can escape the projected
obstruction module.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 13.F10r-c: No Zero-Gap Sequence Escapes The Projection

Every possible zero-gap sequence has a nontrivial projection into the
finite-energy, bounded-Casimir, low-response-height collar module.

Suppose a cofinal active sequence satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
\eta_{\alpha}
\right\|_{OS}
=1,
\qquad
\left\|
P_{\alpha}^{act}{\mathsf T}_{\alpha}P_{\alpha}^{act}
\eta_{\alpha}
\right\|_{OS}
\to
1.
}
$$

Then, for every tolerance:

$$
\boxed{
\delta>0,
}
$$

there are choices:

$$
\boxed{
E,
\qquad
M,
\qquad
R(E,M)
}
$$

fixed before the spectral conclusion, such that:

$$
\boxed{
\liminf_{\alpha}
\left\|
\Pi_{\alpha,E,M}^{act}
\eta_{\alpha}
\right\|_{OS}
\ge
1-\delta.
}
$$

Proof.  Lemma 13.F10r-c0 first proves that any active zero-gap candidate is
captured by the finite projected row-obstruction module up to an arbitrarily
small cofinal error.  The present lemma records the corresponding norm
estimate in the single-collar notation used by the frame argument.

The finite OS transfer operator is a contraction.  The finite spectral
calculus gives:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
\left(
I-P_{\alpha,E}^{collar}
\right)
{\mathsf T}_{\alpha}(t_0)
\right\|_{OS}
\le
\exp(-Et_0).
}
$$

Choose the energy window so this term is below the required tolerance.  Then
choose the response-height and Casimir cutoffs so that Lemma 13.F10r-a makes
the discarded low-energy collar tail below the remaining tolerance.  If the
projection norm were still bounded away from one, the contraction estimate
would force the transfer norm of the sequence to be bounded away from one.
That contradicts the assumed zero-gap behavior.

Lemma 13.F10r-c0 rules out the remaining escape channel: a delocalized,
multi-collar, center, topological, or infrared zero-gap sequence with no
single projected obstruction component.  Such a sequence would have zero
sector-complete response and would be Ward, vacuum, or typed by Lemma 10.1.
Thus the later finite-frame and Schur estimates may be proved on the
projected module without losing a possible zero-gap state.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 13.F10j: Uniform Frame Weighting From Sector Separation

The gap-response packet can be weighted so that it gives uniform finite-frame
bounds on the projected active collar module of Lemmas 13.F10r-a and
13.F10r-b.  The high-height, high-Casimir, and high-energy complements are
already charged to the transfer tail by Lemma 13.F10r-c.

There is a positive response floor on the active collar unit sphere:

$$
\boxed{
\inf_{\eta\in{\mathbb S}_{\alpha,E,M}^{act,collar}}
\sup_{q\in{\mathcal Q}_{\alpha}^{gap}}
\left|
\left\langle
\zeta_{\alpha,q},
\eta
\right\rangle_{OS}
\right|
\ge
d_H
>0.
}
$$

where:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathbb S}_{\alpha,E,M}^{act,collar}
=
\left\{
\eta\in
{\mathcal K}_{\alpha,E,M}^{act,collar}
:
\left\|
\eta
\right\|_{OS}=1
\right\}.
}
$$

Proof of the response floor.  If the displayed floor failed, there would be a
cofinal OS-unit projected active collar sequence whose response against every
gap-response packet element tends to zero.  Lemmas 9.D0a, 9.D1a, 9.D1, 9.0,
9.1, and 10.1 classify such a sequence as Ward, vacuum, or typed.  This
contradicts membership in the projected active collar quotient.

Now use the finite-dimensional frame selection theorem on:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal K}_{\alpha,E,M}^{act,collar}.
}
$$

Because Lemma 13.F10r-b gives:

$$
\boxed{
\dim
{\mathcal K}_{\alpha,E,M}^{act,collar}
\le
n_H(E,M),
}
$$

the constants in the finite frame selection theorem are uniform in the
cutoff.  There are predeclared nonnegative weights:

$$
\boxed{
w_{\alpha,q}\ge0
}
$$

depending only on the cutoff packet and not on any Wilson or spectral
predicate, such that:

$$
\boxed{
a_H
\left\|
\eta
\right\|_{OS}^{2}
\le
\sum_{q\in{\mathcal Q}_{\alpha}^{gap}}
w_{\alpha,q}
\left|
\left\langle
\zeta_{\alpha,q},
\eta
\right\rangle_{OS}
\right|^{2}
\le
A_H
\left\|
\eta
\right\|_{OS}^{2}.
}
$$

The constants can be chosen cofinally with:

$$
\boxed{
a_H
>0,
\qquad
A_H
<\infty.
}
$$

The lower constant depends only on:

$$
\boxed{
d_H,
\qquad
n_H(E,M).
}
$$

The upper constant depends only on:

$$
\boxed{
n_H(E,M),
\qquad
\sup_q
\left\|
\zeta_{\alpha,q}
\right\|_{OS}^{2}
}
$$

after the response packet is Bessel-normalized.

Proof.  The first part gives a norming finite family of response functionals
on the active collar quotient.  Symmetrize the response vectors by including
both signs and real-imaginary parts.  The polar of their convex hull is
contained in a fixed multiple of the OS unit ball.  Since the dimension is at
most the fixed number printed above, John decomposition gives a finite
weighted quadratic form with lower and upper bounds depending only on the
norming constant and the dimension bound.  The weights are computed from the
finite response packet before any conclusion is tested.

Thus the lower-frame constant cannot disappear merely because the regulator
cutoff increases.

Choose the energy window, Casimir cutoff, and height cutoff once for the
mass-gap audit so that the transfer tail from Lemmas 13.F10r-a and
13.F10r-c is smaller than a fixed fraction of the projected deficit:

$$
\boxed{
\tau_H(E,M)
\le
\frac{\epsilon_{proj}^{gap}}{4}.
}
$$

From this point in Section 13, the symbol:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal H}_{\alpha}^{act,collar}
}
$$

denotes the projected module:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal K}_{\alpha,E,M}^{act,collar}
}
$$

with this fixed choice of energy window, Casimir cutoff, and response-height
cutoff.  The discarded complement is not forgotten; it is included in the
final value of the gap deficit.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 13.F10a0: Cofinal Positivity Of The Active Response Gram

The gap-response packet has a cofinal strictly positive lower frame bound on
the projected active collar quotient.

Here the gap-response packet is the sector-complete response packet restricted
to the projected active transfer collar.  It is not a local-only probe family.

Let the active collar unit sphere be:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathbb S}_{\alpha}^{act,collar}
=
\left\{
\eta\in{\mathcal H}_{\alpha}^{act,collar}
:
\left\|
\eta
\right\|_{OS}=1
\right\}.
}
$$

Let the finite gap-response quadratic form be:

$$
\boxed{
Q_{\alpha}^{gap}(\eta)
=
\sum_{q\in{\mathcal Q}_{\alpha}^{gap}}
w_{\alpha,q}
\left|
\left\langle
\zeta_{\alpha,q},
\eta
\right\rangle_{OS}
\right|^{2}.
}
$$

Equivalently, define the active collar response analysis operator:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal C}_{\alpha}^{gap}
:
{\mathcal H}_{\alpha}^{act,collar}
\to
\ell^{2}
\left(
{\mathcal Q}_{\alpha}^{gap},
w_{\alpha}
\right)
}
$$

by:

$$
\boxed{
\left(
{\mathcal C}_{\alpha}^{gap}\eta
\right)_q
=
w_{\alpha,q}^{1/2}
\left\langle
\zeta_{\alpha,q},
\eta
\right\rangle_{OS}.
}
$$

Then:

$$
\boxed{
Q_{\alpha}^{gap}(\eta)
=
\left\|
{\mathcal C}_{\alpha}^{gap}\eta
\right\|_{\ell^{2}}^{2}.
}
$$

Define the finite active response minimum:

$$
\boxed{
m_{\alpha}^{gap}
=
\inf_{\eta\in{\mathbb S}_{\alpha}^{act,collar}}
Q_{\alpha}^{gap}(\eta).
}
$$

Then:

$$
\boxed{
\liminf_{\alpha}
m_{\alpha}^{gap}
\ge
a_H
>0.
}
$$

Equivalently, the finite response-frame operator satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal F}_{\alpha}^{gap}
\big|_{
{\mathcal H}_{\alpha}^{act,collar}
}
\ge
a_H
P_{\alpha}^{act,collar}
}
$$

cofinally.

Proof.  Lemma 13.F10j supplies a uniform finite-frame weighting of the
gap-response packet on the active collar quotient.  Therefore the displayed
lower frame bound follows directly.  For completeness, here is the
contradiction form of the same argument.

The finite active collar unit sphere is compact at each cutoff, so the
displayed infimum is attained.  Suppose the cofinal lower bound fails.  Then
there is a cofinal sequence of OS-unit active collar vectors with vanishing
gap response:

$$
\boxed{
\eta_{\alpha}
\in
{\mathbb S}_{\alpha}^{act,collar},
\qquad
Q_{\alpha}^{gap}(\eta_{\alpha})
\to0.
}
$$

Equivalently:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
{\mathcal C}_{\alpha}^{gap}\eta_{\alpha}
\right\|_{\ell^{2}}
\to0.
}
$$

The gap-response packet is the restriction of the sector-complete packet to
the transfer collar.  Lemmas 9.D0a, 9.D1a, 9.D1, 9.0, and 9.1 say that the
packet norm has the same cofinal zero sets as the full sector norm on bounded
gauge-invariant OS matrix elements.  Vanishing gap response against this
packet eliminates every local, center, topological, and infrared distinction
from vacuum.  Lemma 10.1 classifies the sequence as Ward, vacuum, or typed.

But the active collar quotient has already removed Ward directions, vacuum
directions, and typed extensions.  Therefore an OS-unit vector in that
quotient cannot have vanishing sector-complete response.  This contradiction
proves the cofinal lower frame bound.

At fixed cutoff, the same argument also proves:

$$
\boxed{
\ker
{\mathcal C}_{\alpha}^{gap}
\cap
{\mathcal H}_{\alpha}^{act,collar}
=
\{0\}.
}
$$

The cofinal lower bound is the quantitative strengthening of this kernel
statement.  If the quantitative bound failed, compactness of the finite unit
spheres would produce the vanishing cofinal sequence above, and the same
sector-separation contradiction would apply.

Now choose any preliminary OS-orthonormal finite basis of the active collar
quotient:

$$
\boxed{
\left\{
f_{\alpha,i}
\right\}_{i=1}^{n_{\alpha}}.
}
$$

The response analysis matrix in this preliminary basis is:

$$
\boxed{
\widetilde B_{\alpha}(q,i)
=
w_{\alpha,q}^{1/2}
\left\langle
\zeta_{\alpha,q},
f_{\alpha,i}
\right\rangle_{OS}.
}
$$

Its response Gram matrix is:

$$
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathsf R}_{\alpha}^{resp}
=
\widetilde B_{\alpha}^{*}
\widetilde B_{\alpha}.
}
$$

The lower frame bound is exactly the finite eigenvalue certificate:

$$
\boxed{
\lambda_{\min}
\left(
\widetilde{\mathsf R}_{\alpha}^{resp}
\right)
\ge
a_H.
}
$$

Run finite complete Cholesky or QR pivoting on this positive Gram matrix.
Since the least eigenvalue is bounded below cofinally, no active direction is
discarded by the pivot.  The cofinal residual certificate is:

$$
\boxed{
\delta_H^{2}
\le
a_H.
}
$$

When the same basis is rewritten in any finite collar coordinate family with
OS Gram matrix:

$$
\boxed{
G_{\alpha}^{OS},
}
$$

and response coefficient Gram:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathsf R}_{\alpha}^{resp},
}
$$

the invariant matrix statement is the generalized Gram inequality:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathsf R}_{\alpha}^{resp}
\ge
a_H
G_{\alpha}^{OS}.
}
$$

Thus the Cholesky residual certificate in Lemma 13.F10a is not an additional
admissibility condition.  It is the finite matrix form of sector-complete
response separation on the active OS collar quotient.

$$
\square
$$

### Lemma 13.F10a: OS-Orthonormal Active Collar Basis

At finite cutoff, the projected active transfer restriction from Lemmas
13.F10r-a and 13.F10r-b admits an orthonormal matrix representation in the physical OS
Hilbert norm, and its positive Schur envelope is extracted in that same norm.
The complement is controlled by the transfer tail fixed in Lemma 13.F10j.

Let the finite active collar vectors be:

$$
\boxed{
\xi_{\alpha,u}
\in
{\mathcal H}_{\alpha}^{phys}.
}
$$

Choose a response-pivoted independent active collar subfamily:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal I}_{\alpha}^{act}
\subset
{\mathcal U}_{\alpha}^{collar}.
}
$$

The choice is made by finite QR pivoting in the sector-complete response norm
and is fixed before any spectral predicate is evaluated.  A collar vector is
retained only if its response residual satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}_{\mathcal R}
\left(
\xi_{\alpha,u},
\operatorname{span}
\{\xi_{\alpha,v}:v\hbox{ previously retained}\}
\right)
\ge
\delta_H
>0.
}
$$

The residual threshold is cofinal and comes from the same response floor used
in Lemma 10.1.  The retained family spans the active collar subspace:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal H}_{\alpha}^{act,collar}
=
\operatorname{span}
\left\{
\xi_{\alpha,u}
:
u\in{\mathcal I}_{\alpha}^{act}
\right\}.
}
$$

For coefficients supported on the pivoted family, set:

$$
\boxed{
\Xi_{\alpha}(c)
=
\sum_{u\in{\mathcal I}_{\alpha}^{act}}
c_u\xi_{\alpha,u}.
}
$$

Let the finite gap-response packet produce OS vectors:

$$
\boxed{
\zeta_{\alpha,q}
=
O_{\alpha,q}\Omega_{\alpha},
\qquad
q\in{\mathcal Q}_{\alpha}^{gap}.
}
$$

Define the finite response-frame operator on the active collar subspace:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal F}_{\alpha}^{gap}
=
\sum_{q\in{\mathcal Q}_{\alpha}^{gap}}
w_{\alpha,q}
\left|
\zeta_{\alpha,q}
\right\rangle
\left\langle
\zeta_{\alpha,q}
\right|.
}
$$

Equivalently, define the finite response analysis matrix:

$$
\boxed{
B_{\alpha}(q,u)
=
w_{\alpha,q}^{1/2}
\left\langle
\zeta_{\alpha,q},
\xi_{\alpha,u}
\right\rangle_{OS}.
}
$$

and its coefficient-space response Gram matrix:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathsf R}_{\alpha}^{resp}
=
B_{\alpha}^{*}B_{\alpha}.
}
$$

The response packet is Bessel-normalized before pivoting:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
{\mathsf R}_{\alpha}^{resp}
\right\|_{\ell^{2}\to\ell^{2}}
\le
A_R
<\infty.
}
$$

The pivoted active family is retained only after the finite Cholesky residual
certificate:

$$
\boxed{
\lambda_{\min}
\left(
{\mathsf R}_{\alpha}^{resp}
\big|_{
{\mathcal I}_{\alpha}^{act}
}
\right)
\ge
\delta_H^{2}.
}
$$

This certificate is supplied by Lemma 13.F10a0.  It is not a posterior
selection rule.  The symbols above denote the finite QR-pivoted collar
vectors after the response Gram certificate has been applied, not arbitrary
raw local generators.

The sector-complete response packet gives cofinal frame bounds:

$$
\boxed{
a_H P_{\alpha}^{act,collar}
\le
{\mathcal F}_{\alpha}^{gap}
\le
A_H P_{\alpha}^{act,collar},
\qquad
0<a_H\le A_H<\infty.
}
$$

Equivalently:

$$
\boxed{
a_H
\left\|
\Xi_{\alpha}(c)
\right\|_{OS}^{2}
\le
\sum_{q\in{\mathcal Q}_{\alpha}^{gap}}
w_{\alpha,q}
\left|
\left\langle
\zeta_{\alpha,q},
\Xi_{\alpha}(c)
\right\rangle_{OS}
\right|^{2}
\le
A_H
\left\|
\Xi_{\alpha}(c)
\right\|_{OS}^{2}.
}
$$

For this pivoted family, the OS Gram matrix is:

$$
\boxed{
G_{\alpha}^{OS}(u,v)
=
\left\langle
\xi_{\alpha,u},
\xi_{\alpha,v}
\right\rangle_{OS}.
}
$$

The response-pivoting plus the frame bounds give cofinal Riesz bounds:

$$
\boxed{
0<c_{H}
\le
G_{\alpha}^{OS}
\le
C_{H}
<\infty.
}
$$

The constants are explicit:

$$
\boxed{
c_H
=
\frac{\delta_H^{2}}{A_H},
\qquad
C_H
=
\frac{A_R}{a_H}.
}
$$

Define the OS-orthonormal collar basis by:

$$
\boxed{
e_{\alpha,i}
=
\sum_u
\left(
G_{\alpha}^{OS}
\right)^{-1/2}_{iu}
\xi_{\alpha,u}.
}
$$

Then:

$$
\boxed{
\left\langle
e_{\alpha,i},
e_{\alpha,j}
\right\rangle_{OS}
=
\delta_{ij}.
}
$$

The projected active transfer matrix in the physical Hilbert norm is:

$$
\boxed{
M_{\alpha}(i,j)
=
\left\langle
e_{\alpha,i},
P_{\alpha}^{act}{\mathsf T}_{\alpha}P_{\alpha}^{act}
e_{\alpha,j}
\right\rangle_{OS}.
}
$$

Let the positive row kernel from Lemma 11.4 be:

$$
\boxed{
K_{\alpha}^{gap}(u,v).
}
$$

The OS-Schur envelope is:

$$
\boxed{
S_{\alpha}^{gap}(i,j)
=
\sum_{u,v}
\left|
\left(
G_{\alpha}^{OS}
\right)^{-1/2}_{iu}
\right|
K_{\alpha}^{gap}(u,v)
\left|
\left(
G_{\alpha}^{OS}
\right)^{-1/2}_{vj}
\right|.
}
$$

It satisfies the entrywise domination in the orthonormal OS basis:

$$
\boxed{
\left|
M_{\alpha}(i,j)
\right|
\le
S_{\alpha}^{gap}(i,j).
}
$$

Moreover the Riesz constants only change the row deficit by a fixed finite
collar factor already included in the gap-row envelope:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_i
\sum_j
S_{\alpha}^{gap}(i,j)
\frac{r_{\alpha}(j)}{r_{\alpha}(i)}
\le
1-\epsilon_{*}^{gap}.
}
$$

The reversed collar estimate also holds:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_j
\sum_i
S_{\alpha}^{gap}(i,j)
\frac{r_{\alpha}(i)}{r_{\alpha}(j)}
\le
1-\epsilon_{*}^{gap}.
}
$$

Proof.  Reflection positivity gives the finite OS pre-Hilbert space, and the
null quotient gives a genuine finite Hilbert space.  The active collar
vectors span the non-vacuum singlet transfer sector used in Lemma 13.0 after
Ward, vacuum, and typed directions are removed.

The pivoted family is chosen in the finite response norm.  The response
packet is sector-complete by Lemmas 9.0, 9.1, and 10.1.  Lemma 13.F10a0
turns that separation statement into the cofinal positive response Gram
certificate on the active OS collar quotient.

The upper frame bound follows from bounded finite response-packet operator
norms on a fixed local collar and compact group variables.  The pivoted QR
choice prevents coefficient-space overcompleteness: no retained collar vector
has response residual below the cofinal response-packet threshold.  Combining
the response-frame bounds with this pivot rule gives the Riesz constants
directly.

For the lower bound, the Cholesky certificate gives:

$$
\boxed{
c^{*}
{\mathsf R}_{\alpha}^{resp}
c
\ge
\delta_H^{2}
\left\|
c
\right\|_{2}^{2}.
}
$$

The upper frame inequality gives:

$$
\boxed{
c^{*}
{\mathsf R}_{\alpha}^{resp}
c
\le
A_H
c^{*}
G_{\alpha}^{OS}
c.
}
$$

Therefore:

$$
\boxed{
c^{*}
G_{\alpha}^{OS}
c
\ge
\frac{\delta_H^{2}}{A_H}
\left\|
c
\right\|_{2}^{2}.
}
$$

For the upper bound, the Bessel normalization gives:

$$
\boxed{
c^{*}
{\mathsf R}_{\alpha}^{resp}
c
\le
A_R
\left\|
c
\right\|_{2}^{2}.
}
$$

The lower frame inequality gives:

$$
\boxed{
a_H
c^{*}
G_{\alpha}^{OS}
c
\le
c^{*}
{\mathsf R}_{\alpha}^{resp}
c.
}
$$

Therefore:

$$
\boxed{
c_H\left\|c\right\|_2^2
\le
\left\|
\Xi_{\alpha}(c)
\right\|_{OS}^{2}
\le
C_H\left\|c\right\|_2^2.
}
$$

These are exactly the Riesz bounds for:

$$
\boxed{
G_{\alpha}^{OS}.
}
$$

The displayed basis is obtained by applying the inverse square root of the OS
Gram matrix on the active quotient.  Therefore it is orthonormal in the
physical OS norm.  The matrix shown is not formal; it is the matrix of the
operator:

$$
\boxed{
P_{\alpha}^{act}{\mathsf T}_{\alpha}P_{\alpha}^{act}
}
$$

on the finite physical Hilbert space.

Lemma 11.4 supplies the positive gap-row kernel before orthonormalization.
Conjugating by the bounded inverse square root of the OS Gram matrix gives
the printed Schur envelope.  The cofinal Riesz bounds ensure that this
conjugation changes the envelope by only fixed finite collar constants.  The
height function is chosen after this OS normalization, so those constants are
absorbed into the printed gap-row deficit rather than into the final
spectral answer.

Thus the Schur envelope is an envelope in the actual OS norm.

$$
\square
$$
